10.1 Caching Fundamentals and Benefits

What is Caching?

Caching is the practice of storing copies of data in a high-speed storage layer (the cache) so that future requests for that data can be served faster than accessing the primary storage location. It exploits the principle of locality of reference - the observation that recently accessed data is likely to be accessed again soon.

Cache Terminology

TermDefinitionExample
Cache HitRequested data found in cacheUser profile loaded from Redis
Cache MissData not in cache, must fetch from sourceFirst-time product lookup
Hit Rate/RatioPercentage of requests served from cache95% hit rate
TTL (Time To Live)Duration data remains valid in cache3600 seconds
EvictionRemoving data from cacheLRU removing oldest entry
InvalidationMarking cached data as staleProduct price changed
Cache WarmingPre-populating cache before trafficLoading popular products at startup
Cache StampedeMany requests hitting backend simultaneouslyCache expires, 1000 requests hit DB
Stale DataCached data that's out of sync with sourceOld price shown briefly
Cache PenetrationRequests for non-existent data bypassing cacheQuerying invalid user IDs

10.2 Cache Placement Strategies

The Caching Layers

Modern applications can implement caching at multiple layers, each with distinct characteristics and trade-offs:

Pattern 1: Cache-Aside (Lazy Loading)

The most commonly used pattern where the application is responsible for maintaining the cache.

Cache-Aside Characteristics:

AspectDetails
ProsSimple to implement, application has full control, resilient to cache failures
ConsApplication complexity, potential inconsistency window, cache stampede risk
Best ForRead-heavy workloads, general-purpose caching
ConsistencyEventual (brief window of stale data possible)

Pattern 2: Read-Through Cache

The cache sits between the application and database, automatically loading data on cache misses.

Pattern 4: Write-Behind (Write-Back) Cache

Writes are acknowledged immediately after updating cache, then asynchronously persisted to database.

10.4 Cache Invalidation Strategies

The Hardest Problem in Caching

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   "There are only two hard things in Computer Science:                      â”‚
â”‚    cache invalidation and naming things."                                   â”‚
â”‚                                        â€” Phil Karlton                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

Cache invalidation is challenging because you must balance freshness (serving up-to-date data) with performance (minimizing cache misses) and complexity (keeping the system maintainable).

Invalidation Strategies Overview

10.9 Cache Warming and Preloading

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚               KEY TAKEAWAYS - SECTION 10: CACHING ARCHITECTURE               â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤

â”‚   FUNDAMENTALS:                                                             â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Caching trades memory for speed - store frequently accessed            â”‚
â”‚      data closer to where it's needed                                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Cache at multiple layers (browser â†’ CDN â†’ gateway â†’ app â†’              â”‚
â”‚      distributed cache â†’ database) for maximum benefit                      â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Understand the memory hierarchy - each layer has different             â”‚
â”‚      latency, capacity, and cost characteristics                            â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   PATTERNS:                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Cache-Aside: Application manages cache, most flexible,                 â”‚
â”‚      use as default pattern                                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Read-Through/Write-Through: Cache manages data loading,                â”‚
â”‚      simpler application code                                               â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Write-Behind: Async writes for high throughput,                        â”‚
â”‚      accepts eventual consistency                                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Refresh-Ahead: Proactive refresh for predictable patterns,             â”‚
â”‚      eliminates cache miss latency                                          â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   INVALIDATION:                                                             â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… "Cache invalidation is one of the hardest problems" -                  â”‚
â”‚      plan your strategy carefully                                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… TTL-based: Simple but may serve stale data                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Event-based: Real-time but complex                                     â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Version-based: No explicit invalidation but orphaned entries           â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Hybrid: Combine strategies for best results                            â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   DISTRIBUTED CACHING:                                                      â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                      â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Use consistent hashing to minimize redistribution when                 â”‚
â”‚      scaling cluster                                                        â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Handle hot keys with replication, local caching, or key splitting      â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Prevent cache stampede with locking, jittered TTL, or                  â”‚
â”‚      stale-while-revalidate                                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Protect against cache penetration with null caching or bloom filters   â”‚

â”‚   EVICTION:                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… LRU: Good default for most workloads                                   â”‚
â”‚   âœ… LFU: Better for stable access patterns                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… W-TinyLFU (Caffeine): Near-optimal for varied workloads                â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Add jitter to TTL to prevent thundering herd                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚

â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                              â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Use CDN for static assets and geographically distributed users         â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Leverage Cache-Control headers for fine-grained caching control        â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚

â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Use cache busting (versioned URLs) for instant updates                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   BEST PRACTICES:                                                           â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                           â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Design cache keys that are descriptive, namespaced, and versioned      â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Cache should never be a single point of failure -                      â”‚
â”‚      implement graceful degradation                                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Monitor hit rate (target >90%), latency, memory, and evictions         â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Implement cache warming for predictable cold start behavior            â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Consider security: don't leak user data across cache entries           â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚   PITFALLS TO AVOID:                                                        â”‚
â”‚   â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•                                                        â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Caching everything (low hit rate, wasted memory)                       â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Ignoring cache consistency (stale data issues)                         â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Using cache as primary data store (data loss risk)                     â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Not handling cache failures (cascading failures)                       â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Ignoring thundering herd (database overload)                           â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Cache pollution from batch jobs (evicting hot data)                    â”‚

â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€        â”‚

â”‚   Static assets                     â”‚ CDN + long TTL + cache busting        â”‚

â”‚   Hot data, low latency             â”‚ Local cache (Caffeine)                â”‚
â”‚   Unknown workload                  â”‚ W-TinyLFU or ARC                      â”‚
â”‚   API responses (public)            â”‚ CDN + gateway cache                   â”‚
â”‚   Real-time data                    â”‚ Short TTL or no cache                 â”‚
